           </li>

      <tr>
       <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">
        <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
         <ul>
          <li class="nv-view">
           <a href="/wiki/Template:Eschatology" title="Template:Eschatology">
            <span title="View this template">
             v
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="nv-talk">
           <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Eschatology" title="Template talk:Eschatology">
            <span title="Discuss this template">
             t
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="nv-edit">
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Eschatology&amp;action=edit">
            <span title="Edit this template">
             e
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </div>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      <b>
       End time
      </b>
      (also called
      <b>
       end times
      </b>
      ,
      <b>
       end of time
      </b>
      ,
      <b>
       end of days
      </b>
      ,
      <b>
       last days
      </b>
      ,
      <b>
       final days
      </b>
      , or
      <b>
       eschaton
      </b>
      ) is a time period described in the
      <a href="/wiki/Eschatology" title="Eschatology">
       eschatologies
      </a>
      of the dominant
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_religion" title="World religion">
       world religions
      </a>
      , both
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abrahamic_religion" title="Abrahamic religion">
       Abrahamic
      </a>
      and non-Abrahamic.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abrahamic_faiths" title="Abrahamic faiths">
       Abrahamic faiths
      </a>
      maintain a linear
      <a href="/wiki/Cosmology" title="Cosmology">
       cosmology
      </a>
      , with end-time scenarios containing themes of
      <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_transformation" title="Spiritual transformation">
       transformation
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Redemption_(theology)" title="Redemption (theology)">
       redemption
      </a>
      . In
      <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">
       Judaism
      </a>
      , the term "end of days" makes reference to the
      <a href="/wiki/Messianic_Age" title="Messianic Age">
       Messianic Age
      </a>
      , and includes an in-gathering of the exiled
      <a href="/wiki/Diaspora" title="Diaspora">
       diaspora
      </a>
      , the coming of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_Messiah" title="Jewish Messiah">
       Messiah
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Techiyat_hamaysim" title="Techiyat hamaysim">
       resurrection of the righteous
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_eschatology#.22The_world_to_come.22" title="Jewish eschatology">
       the world to come
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
       Christianity
      </a>
      traditionally depicts the end time as a period of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tribulation" title="Tribulation">
       tribulation
      </a>
      that precedes the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Coming" title="Second Coming">
       second coming
      </a>
      of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ" title="Jesus Christ">
       Christ
      </a>
      , who will face the emergence of the
      <a href="/wiki/Antichrist" title="Antichrist">
       Antichrist
      </a>
      and usher in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_God" title="Kingdom of God">
       Kingdom of God
      </a>
      . However, some Christians believe that the end time represents the personal tribulation experienced before they are enlightened with the
      <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Word_of_God" title="Word of God">
       Word of God
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In Islam, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yawm_al-Qiy%C4%81mah" title="Yawm al-Qiymah">
       Day of Judgement
      </a>
      is preceded by the appearance of the
      <a href="/wiki/Mahdi" title="Mahdi">
       Mahdi
      </a>
      atop a white stallion. With the help of
      <a href="/wiki/Jesus_in_Islam" title="Jesus in Islam">
       Isa
      </a>
      (Jesus), the Mahdi will then triumph over
      <a href="/wiki/Masih_ad-Dajjal" title="Masih ad-Dajjal">
       Masih ad-Dajjal
      </a>
      (the false messiah).
     </p>
     <p>
      Non-Abrahamic faiths tend to have more cyclical world-views, with end-time eschatologies characterized by
      <a href="/wiki/Social_disintegration" title="Social disintegration">
       decay
      </a>
      , redemption and rebirth. In
      <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">
       Hinduism
      </a>
      , end time is foretold
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
         <span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (October 2014)">
          by whom?
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      as when
      <a href="/wiki/Kalki" title="Kalki">
       Kalki
      </a>
      , the final incarnation of
      <a href="/wiki/Vishnu" title="Vishnu">
       Vishnu
      </a>
      , descends atop a white horse and brings an end to the current
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Kali_Yuga" title="Kali Yuga">
        Kali Yuga
       </a>
      </i>
      . In
      <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
       Buddhism
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddha" title="Buddha">
       Buddha
      </a>
      predicted that his teachings would be forgotten after 5,000 years, followed by turmoil. A
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Bodhisattva" title="Bodhisattva">
        bodhisattva
       </a>
      </i>
      named
      <a href="/wiki/Maitreya" title="Maitreya">
       Maitreya
      </a>
      will appear and rediscover the teaching of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Dharma" title="Dharma">
        dharma
       </a>
      </i>
      . The ultimate destruction of the world will then come through seven suns.
     </p>
     <p>
      Since the discovery of
      <a href="/wiki/Deep_time" title="Deep time">
       deep time
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Age_of_the_Earth" title="Age of the Earth">
       age of the Earth
      </a>
      , scientific discourse about end time has centered on the
      <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_fate_of_the_universe" title="Ultimate fate of the universe">
       ultimate fate of the universe
      </a>
      . Theories have included the
      <a href="/wiki/Big_Rip" title="Big Rip">
       Big Rip
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Big_Crunch" title="Big Crunch">
       Big Crunch
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Big_Bounce" title="Big Bounce">
       Big Bounce
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Freeze" title="Big Freeze">
       Big Freeze
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Linear_cosmology">
       Linear cosmology
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Linear cosmology">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Zoroastrianism">
       Zoroastrianism
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Zoroastrianism">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Frashokereti" title="Frashokereti">
       Frashokereti
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Zoroastrian eschatology is the oldest in recorded history, with beliefs paralleling and predating the framework of the major Abrahamic faiths.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      By the year 500 BC, a fully developed concept of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/End_of_the_world_(disambiguation)" title="End of the world (disambiguation)">
       end of the world
      </a>
      was established in Zoroastrianism. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahman_Yasht" title="Bahman Yasht">
       Bahman Yasht
      </a>
      describes:
     </p>
     <blockquote>
      <p>
       At the end of thy tenth hundredth winter, the
       <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">
        sun
       </a>
       is more unseen and more spotted; the year, month, and day are shorter; and the earth is more barren; and the crop will not yield the seed. And men become more deceitful and more given to vile practices. They will have no gratitude. Honorable wealth will proceed to those of perverted faith. And a dark cloud makes the whole sky night, and it will rain more noxious creatures than water.
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      A
      <a href="/wiki/Manichaeism" title="Manichaeism">
       Manichaean
      </a>
      battle between the righteous and wicked will be followed by the
      <a href="/wiki/Frashokereti" title="Frashokereti">
       Frashokereti
      </a>
      . On earth, the
      <a href="/wiki/Saoshyant" title="Saoshyant">
       Saoshyant
      </a>
      will arrive as the final savior of mankind, and bring about the
      <a href="/wiki/Resurrection_of_the_dead" title="Resurrection of the dead">
       resurrection of the dead
      </a>
      . The
      <i>
       yazata
      </i>
      s
      <a href="/wiki/Airyaman" title="Airyaman">
       Airyaman
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Atar" title="Atar">
       Atar
      </a>
      will melt the metal in the hills and mountains, which will flow as lava across the earth and all mankind, both the living and resurrected, will be required to wade through it.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Ashavan" title="Ashavan">
        Ashavan
       </a>
      </i>
      will pass through the molten river as if it were warm milk, but the sinful will burn. It will then flow down to hell, where it will annihilate
      <a href="/wiki/Angra_Mainyu" title="Angra Mainyu">
       Angra Mainyu
      </a>
      and the last vestiges of wickedness.
     </p>
     <p>
      The righteous will partake of the
      <i>
       parahaoma
      </i>
      , which will confer immortality upon them. Humanity will become like the
      <a href="/wiki/Amesha_Spenta" title="Amesha Spenta">
       Amesha Spentas
      </a>
      , living without food, hunger, thirst, weapons or injury. Bodies will become so light as to cast no shadow. All humanity will speak a single language, and belong to a single nation with no borders. All will share a single purpose and goal, joining with
      <a href="/wiki/Ahura_Mazda" title="Ahura Mazda">
       Ahura Mazda
      </a>
      for a perpetual and divine exaltation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boyce_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Boyce-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Judaism">
       Judaism
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Judaism">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_eschatology" title="Jewish eschatology">
       Jewish eschatology
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In Judaism, the main textual source for the belief in the end of days and accompanying events is the Tanakh or Hebrew Bible. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Five_Books_of_Moses" title="Five Books of Moses">
       Five Books of Moses
      </a>
      (the Torah) describe a time when the Jewish people will not be able to keep the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laws_of_Moses" title="Laws of Moses">
       Laws of Moses
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Israel" title="Land of Israel">
       Land of Israel
      </a>
      , and will be exiled but ultimately redeemed. The main sources are the book of
      <a href="/wiki/Isaiah" title="Isaiah">
       Isaiah
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jeremiah" title="Jeremiah">
       Jeremiah
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ezekiel" title="Ezekiel">
       Ezekiel
      </a>
      . The books of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hebrew_Prophets" title="Hebrew Prophets">
       Hebrew Prophets
      </a>
      also elaborate about the end of days.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jewish_Eschatology_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jewish_Eschatology-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Rabbinic_literature" title="Rabbinic literature">
       rabbinic literature
      </a>
      , rabbis elaborated and explained the prophecies that were found in the Hebrew Bible, along with
      <a href="/wiki/Oral_law" title="Oral law">
       oral law
      </a>
      and rabbinic traditions about its significance.
     </p>
     <p>
      The main tenets of Jewish eschatology are the following, in no particular order:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jewish_Eschatology_7-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jewish_Eschatology-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       God will redeem Israel from the captivity that began during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babylonian_Exile" title="Babylonian Exile">
        Babylonian Exile
       </a>
       in a new
       <a href="/wiki/The_Exodus" title="The Exodus">
        Exodus
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       God will return the Jewish people to the
       <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Israel" title="Land of Israel">
        Land of Israel
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       God will restore the
       <a href="/wiki/Davidic_line" title="Davidic line">
        House of David
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Third_Temple" title="The Third Temple">
        Temple in Jerusalem
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       God will raise up a regent from the House of David, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_Messiah" title="Jewish Messiah">
        Jewish Messiah
       </a>
       , to lead the Jewish people and the world and usher in an
       <a href="/wiki/Messianic_Age" title="Messianic Age">
        age of justice and peace
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       Nations will recognize that the
       <a href="/wiki/God_in_Judaism" title="God in Judaism">
        God of Israel
       </a>
       is the only true god
      </li>
      <li>
       God will
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resurrection_of_the_Dead" title="Resurrection of the Dead">
        resurrect the dead
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       God will create a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_to_Come#Judaism" title="World to Come">
        new heaven and earth
       </a>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      It is also believed that history will complete itself, and the ultimate destination will be reached as all mankind returns to the
      <a href="/wiki/Garden_of_Eden" title="Garden of Eden">
       Garden of Eden
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Tribulation_and_the_Messianic_Age">
       Tribulation and the Messianic Age
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Tribulation and the Messianic Age">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Messianic_Age" title="Messianic Age">
       Messianic Age
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Most of tenets of Jewish eschatology are in the
      <a href="/wiki/Nevi%27im" title="Nevi'im">
       Nevi'im
      </a>
      , primarily in the books of
      <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Isaiah" title="Book of Isaiah">
       Isaiah
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Jeremiah" title="Book of Jeremiah">
       Jeremiah
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Ezekiel" title="Book of Ezekiel">
       Ezekiel
      </a>
      . Moses foretells the end of days in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deuteronomy" title="Deuteronomy">
       Deuteronomy
      </a>
      , describing a time of
      <a href="/wiki/Apostasy" title="Apostasy">
       apostasy
      </a>
      , in which people of Israel become "settled upon their lees". They do not keep the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laws_of_Moses" title="Laws of Moses">
       Laws of Moses
      </a>
      and resort to idolatry.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jewish_Eschatology_7-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jewish_Eschatology-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       [You will] corrupt yourselves, and make a graven image, or the likeness of any thing, and shall do evil in the sight of the Lord thy God, to provoke him to anger: 26 I call heaven and earth to witness against you this day, that ye shall soon utterly perish from off the land whereunto ye go over Jordan to possess it; ye shall not prolong your days upon it, but shall utterly be destroyed. 27 And the Lord shall scatter you among the nations, and ye shall be left few in number among the heathen, whither the Lord shall lead you. 28 And there ye shall serve gods, the work of men's hands, wood and stone, which neither see, nor hear, nor eat, nor smell.
      </p>
      <div class="templatequotecite">
       
       <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap">
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Deuteronomy+4%3A25%E2%80%9328&amp;version=ESV" rel="nofollow">
         Deuteronomy 4:2528
        </a>
       </span>
       KJV
      </div>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      The Book of Isaiah also describes a time of judgment in
      <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap">
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Isaiah+2%3A4&amp;version=ESV" rel="nofollow">
        Isaiah 2:4
       </a>
      </span>
      : "And he shall judge among the nations, and shall rebuke many people."
     </p>
     <p>
      The Messianic Age will follow, and will be an era of global peace, free of strife, and conducive to knowledge of the creator. This is described in a famous scriptural passage from the Book of Isaiah,
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       They shall beat their swords into plowshares and their spears into pruning hooks; nation will not lift sword against nation and they will no longer study warfare".
      </p>
      <div class="templatequotecite">
       
       <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap">
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Isaiah+2%3A4&amp;version=ESV" rel="nofollow">
         Isaiah 2:4
        </a>
       </span>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jewish_Eschatology_7-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Jewish_Eschatology-7">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         7
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </div>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Maimonides" title="Maimonides">
       Maimonides
      </a>
      further describes the Messianic Era in the
      <a href="/wiki/Mishneh_Torah" title="Mishneh Torah">
       Mishneh Torah
      </a>
      :
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       And at that time there will be no hunger or war, no jealousy or rivalry. For the good will be plentiful, and all delicacies available as dust. The entire occupation of the world will be only to know God... the people Israel will be of great wisdom; they will perceive the esoteric truths and comprehend their Creator's wisdom as is the capacity of man. As it is written (Isaiah 11:9): "For the earth shall be filled with the knowledge of God, as the waters cover the sea.
      </p>
      <div class="templatequotecite">
       Mishneh Torah, Laws of Kings 12:5
      </div>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/Talmud" title="Talmud">
       Talmud
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the
      <a href="/wiki/Midrash" title="Midrash">
       Midrash
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rabbi_Eliezer_1981.2C_p._141_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rabbi_Eliezer_1981.2C_p._141-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the medieval
      <a href="/wiki/Kabbalah" title="Kabbalah">
       kabbalistic
      </a>
      work, the
      <a href="/wiki/Zohar" title="Zohar">
       Zohar
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the messiah must arrive before the
      <a href="/wiki/Year_6000" title="Year 6000">
       year 6000
      </a>
      from the
      <a href="/wiki/Anno_Mundi" title="Anno Mundi">
       time of creation
      </a>
      , or before the year 2240 AD. The
      <a href="/wiki/Midrash" title="Midrash">
       Midrash
      </a>
      comments, "Six eons for going in and coming out, for war and peace. The seventh eon is entirely Shabbat and rest for life everlasting."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rabbi_Eliezer_1981.2C_p._141_10-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rabbi_Eliezer_1981.2C_p._141-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Zohar
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      maintains that the seven days of the week, based on the seven days of creation, correspond to the seven millennia of creation. The seventh day of the week, the
      <a href="/wiki/Shabbat" title="Shabbat">
       Shabbat
      </a>
      day of rest, corresponds to the seventh millennium, the age of universal
      <b>
       rest
      </b>
      , or the Messianic Era. The seventh millennium begins with the year 6000
      <a href="/wiki/Anno_Mundi" title="Anno Mundi">
       AM
      </a>
      , and is the latest time the Messiah can come. There are a number of early and late Jewish scholars that have written in support of this, including the
      <a href="/wiki/Nahmanides" title="Nahmanides">
       Ramban
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isaac_Abrabanel" title="Isaac Abrabanel">
       Isaac Abrabanel
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abraham_Ibn_Ezra" title="Abraham Ibn Ezra">
       Abraham Ibn Ezra
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Rabbeinu
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bachya" title="Bachya">
       Bachya
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the
      <a href="/wiki/Vilna_Gaon" title="Vilna Gaon">
       Vilna Gaon
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lubavitcher_Rebbe" title="Lubavitcher Rebbe">
       Lubavitcher Rebbe
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ramchal" title="Ramchal">
       Ramchal
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Aryeh_Kaplan" title="Aryeh Kaplan">
       Aryeh Kaplan
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Rebbetzin
      <a href="/wiki/Esther_Jungreis" title="Esther Jungreis">
       Esther Jungreis
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>

        ]
       </span>
      </span>

            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            <a href="/wiki/Two_witnesses" title="Two witnesses">
             Two witnesses
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            <a href="/wiki/War_in_Heaven" title="War in Heaven">
             War in Heaven
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            <a href="/wiki/Whore_of_Babylon" title="Whore of Babylon">
             Whore of Babylon
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_to_Come" title="World to Come">
             World to Come
            </a>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </div>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;">
        <a href="/wiki/Portal:Christianity" title="Portal:Christianity">
         Christianity portal
        </a>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">
        <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
         <ul>
          <li class="nv-view">
           <a href="/wiki/Template:Christian_eschatology" title="Template:Christian eschatology">
            <span title="View this template">
             v
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="nv-talk">
           <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Christian_eschatology" title="Template talk:Christian eschatology">
            <span title="Discuss this template">
             t
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="nv-edit">
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Christian_eschatology&amp;action=edit">
            <span title="Edit this template">
             e
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </div>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Coming" title="Second Coming">
       Second Coming
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Christian_eschatology" title="Christian eschatology">
       Christian eschatology
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Last_Judgment" title="Last Judgment">
       Last Judgment
      </a>
     </div>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       Date
      </dt>
     </dl>
     <p>
      Some
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_the_1st_century" title="Christianity in the 1st century">
       first century Christians
      </a>
      believed Jesus would return during their lifetime. When the converts of Paul in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thessalonica" title="Thessalonica">
       Thessalonica
      </a>
      were persecuted by the
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
       Roman Empire
      </a>
      , they believed the end of days to be imminent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      While some who believe in the literal interpretation of the Bible insist that the prediction of dates or times is futile, others believe Jesus foretold signs of the end of days. The precise time, however, will come like a "thief in the night" (
      <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap">
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=1+Thess.+5%3A2&amp;version=ESV" rel="nofollow">
        1 Thess. 5:2
       </a>
      </span>
      ). They may also refer to
      <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap">
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Matthew+24%3A36&amp;version=ESV" rel="nofollow">
        Matthew 24:36
       </a>
      </span>
      in which Jesus is quoted as saying:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       "But concerning that day and hour no one knows, not even the angels of heaven, nor the Son, but the Father only."
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       Great Tribulation
      </dt>
     </dl>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Abomination_of_desolation" title="Abomination of desolation">
       Abomination of desolation
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Tribulation" title="Great Tribulation">
       Great Tribulation
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The prophetic theme of Tribulation in the New Testament mirrors the Old Testament.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      In the New Testament, Jesus refers to this as the "Great Tribulation"(
      <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap">
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Matthew+24%3A21&amp;version=ESV" rel="nofollow">
        Matthew 24:21
       </a>
      </span>
      ), "Affliction"(
      <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap">
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Mark+13%3A19&amp;version=ESV" rel="nofollow">
        Mark 13:19
       </a>
      </span>
      ), and "days of vengeance"(
      <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap">
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Luke+21%3A22&amp;version=ESV" rel="nofollow">
        Luke 21:22
       </a>
      </span>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      The Book of Matthew describes the devastation:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       When ye therefore shall see the abomination of desolation, spoken of by Daniel the prophet, stand in the holy place, (whoso readeth, let him understand). Then let them which be in Judaea flee into the mountains. Let him which is on the housetop not come down...Neither let him which is in the field return back to take his clothes, and woe unto them that are with child...For then shall be great tribulation, such as was not since the beginning of the world to this time, no, nor ever shall be. And except those days should be shortened, there should no flesh be saved: but for the elect's sake those days shall be shortened.
      </p>
      <div class="templatequotecite">
       
       <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap">
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Matthew+24%3A15%E2%80%9322&amp;version=ESV" rel="nofollow">
         Matthew 24:1522
        </a>
       </span>
      </div>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      The resulting chaos will affect pregnancies, newborns, and a scourge will spread throughout the flesh, save for the elect. The vivid imagery of this section is repeated closely in
      <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap">
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Mark+13%3A14%E2%80%9320&amp;version=ESV" rel="nofollow">
        Mark 13:1420
       </a>
      </span>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The Gospel of Luke describes a complete unraveling of the social fabric, with widespread calamity and war:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       Then he said to them, Nation will rise against nation, and kingdom against kingdom. There will be great earthquakes, and in various places famines and pestilences. And there will be terrors and great signs from heaven. But before all this they will lay their hands on you and persecute you, delivering you up to the synagogues and prisons, and you will be brought before kings and governors for my name's sake. This will be your opportunity to bear witness. Settle it therefore in your minds not to meditate beforehand how to answer, for I will give you a mouth and wisdom, which none of your adversaries will be able to withstand or contradict. You will be delivered up even by parents and brothers and relatives and friends, and some of you they will put to death. You will be hated by all for my name's sake. But not a hair of your head will perish. By your endurance you will gain your lives.
      </p>
      <p>
       But when you see Jerusalem surrounded by armies, then know that its desolation has come near. Then let those who are in Judea flee to the mountains, and let those who are inside the city depart, and let not those who are out in the country enter it, for these are days of vengeance, to fulfill all that is written. Alas for women who are pregnant and for those who are nursing infants in those days! For there will be great distress upon the earth and wrath against this people. They will fall by the edge of the sword and be led captive among all nations, and Jerusalem will be trampled underfoot by the Gentiles, until the times of the Gentiles are fulfilled.
      </p>
      <p>
       And there will be signs in sun and moon and stars, and on the earth distress of nations in perplexity because of the roaring of the sea and the waves, people fainting with fear and with foreboding of what is coming on the world. For the powers of the heavens will be shaken. And then they will see the Son of Man coming in a cloud with power and great glory. Now when these things begin to take place, straighten up and raise your heads, because your redemption is drawing near.
      </p>
      And he told them a parable: Look at the fig tree, and all the trees. As soon as they come out in leaf, you see for yourselves and know that the summer is already near. So also, when you see these things taking place, you know that the kingdom of God is near. Truly, I say to you, this generation will not pass away until all has taken place. Heaven and earth will pass away, but my words will not pass away.
      <div class="templatequotecite">
       
       <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap">
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Luke+21%3A10%E2%80%9333&amp;version=ESV" rel="nofollow">
         Luke 21:1033
        </a>
       </span>
      </div>
     </blockquote>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Catholicism">
       Catholicism
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Catholicism">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Profession_of_faith_(Catholic_Church)" title="Profession of faith (Catholic Church)">
       Profession of Faith
      </a>
      addresses Catholic beliefs concerning the Last Days.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Catholicism adheres to the
      <a href="/wiki/Amillennialism" title="Amillennialism">
       amillennial
      </a>
      school of thought, promoted by
      <a href="/wiki/Augustine_of_Hippo" title="Augustine of Hippo">
       Augustine of Hippo
      </a>
      in his work
      <a href="/wiki/City_of_God_(book)" title="City of God (book)">
       <i>
        The City of God
       </i>
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Protestantism">
       Protestantism
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Protestantism">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Antichrist1.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="543" data-file-width="441" height="271" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Antichrist1.jpg/220px-Antichrist1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Antichrist1.jpg/330px-Antichrist1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Antichrist1.jpg/440px-Antichrist1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Antichrist1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Antichrist, by
        <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Cranach_the_Elder" title="Lucas Cranach the Elder">
         Lucas Cranach the Elder
        </a>
        (1521) Here the
        <a href="/wiki/Antichrist" title="Antichrist">
         Antichrist
        </a>
        is shown wearing the triple crown of the Roman papacy.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Protestants are divided between Millennialists and Amillennialists.
      <a href="/wiki/Millennialism" title="Millennialism">
       Millennialists
      </a>
      concentrate on the issue of whether the true believers will see the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tribulation" title="Tribulation">
       tribulation
      </a>
      or be removed from it by what is referred to as a Pre-Tribulation
      <a href="/wiki/Rapture" title="Rapture">
       Rapture
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Amillennialism" title="Amillennialism">
       Amillennialists
      </a>
      believe that the end times encompass the time from Christ's ascension to the Last day, and maintain that the mention of the "thousand years" in the
      <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Revelation" title="Book of Revelation">
       Book of Revelation
      </a>
      is meant to be taken metaphorically (i.e., not literally, or 'spiritually'), a view which continues to cause divisions within
      <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
       evangelical
      </a>
      Christianity.
     </p>
     <p>
      There is a range of eschatological belief in Protestant Christianity. Christian
      <a href="/wiki/Premillennialism" title="Premillennialism">
       premillennialists
      </a>
      who believe that the End Times are occurring now, are usually specific about timelines that climax in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/End_of_the_world_(religion)" title="End of the world (religion)">
       end of the world
      </a>
      . For some,
      <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
       Israel
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
       European Union
      </a>
      , or the United Nations are seen as major players whose roles were foretold in scripture. Within
      <a href="/wiki/Dispensationalism" title="Dispensationalism">
       dispensational premillennialist
      </a>
      writing, there is the belief that Christians will be summoned to
      <a href="/wiki/Heaven" title="Heaven">
       Heaven
      </a>
      by Christ at the
      <a href="/wiki/Rapture" title="Rapture">
       Rapture
      </a>
      , occurring before a "Great Tribulation" prophesied in Matthew 2425; Mark 13 and Luke 21. The Tribulation is described in the book of Revelation.
     </p>
     <p>
      "End times" may also refer to the passing of an age or long period in the relationship between man and God.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Adherents to this view cite the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Epistle_to_Timothy" title="Second Epistle to Timothy">
       Second Epistle to Timothy
      </a>
      and draw analogies to the late twentieth and early twenty-first centuries.
     </p>
     <p>
      Post-Exilic Hebrew books of
      <a href="/wiki/Prophecy" title="Prophecy">
       prophecy
      </a>
      such as
      <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Daniel" title="Book of Daniel">
       Daniel
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Ezekiel" title="Book of Ezekiel">
       Ezekiel
      </a>
      are given new interpretations in this tradition, while in
      <a href="/wiki/Apocalyptic_literature" title="Apocalyptic literature">
       apocalyptic forecasts
      </a>
      appear in the Judeo-Christian
      <a href="/wiki/Sibylline_Oracles" title="Sibylline Oracles">
       Sibylline Oracles
      </a>
      which include the Book of Revelation ascribed to John, the
      <a href="/wiki/Apocrypha" title="Apocrypha">
       apocryphal
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Apocalypse_of_Peter" title="Apocalypse of Peter">
       Apocalypse of Peter
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/2_Esdras" title="2 Esdras">
       Second Book Of Esdras
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Most fundamentalist Christians anticipate biblical prophecy to be literally fulfilled. They see current wars, natural disaster and famine as the birth pangs which Jesus described in Matthew
      <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/bibleversefinder/?book=Matthew&amp;verse=24:78&amp;src=">
       24:78
      </a>
      and Mark
      <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/bibleversefinder/?book=Mark&amp;verse=13:8&amp;src=">
       13:8
      </a>
      . They believe that mankind began in the
      <a href="/wiki/Garden_of_Eden" title="Garden of Eden">
       garden of Eden
      </a>
      , and point to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megiddo_(place)" title="Megiddo (place)">
       Megiddo
      </a>
      as the place the current
      <a href="/wiki/World-system" title="World-system">
       world system
      </a>
      will finish, after which the Messiah will rule for 1,000 years.
     </p>
     <p>
      Contemporary use of the term
      <i>
       End Times
      </i>
      has evolved from literal belief in Christian
      <a href="/wiki/Millennialism" title="Millennialism">
       millennialism
      </a>
      . In this tradition,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biblical" title="Biblical">
       Biblical
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Apocalypse" title="Apocalypse">
       apocalypse
      </a>
      is believed to be imminent, with various current events as
      <a href="/wiki/Omen" title="Omen">
       omens
      </a>
      of impending
      <a href="/wiki/Armageddon" title="Armageddon">
       Armageddon
      </a>
      . These beliefs have been put forward by the Adventist movement (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Millerites" title="Millerites">
       Millerites
      </a>
      ),
      <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">
       Jehovah's Witnesses
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Dispensationalism" title="Dispensationalism">
       dispensational premillennialists
      </a>
      . In 1918 a group of eight well known preachers produced the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Manifesto" title="London Manifesto">
       London Manifesto
      </a>
      , warning of an imminent second coming of Christ shortly after the 1917 liberation of Jerusalem by the British.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Icon_second_coming.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="770" data-file-width="600" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Icon_second_coming.jpg/220px-Icon_second_coming.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Icon_second_coming.jpg/330px-Icon_second_coming.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Icon_second_coming.jpg/440px-Icon_second_coming.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Icon_second_coming.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Icon of the Second Coming. Greek, ca. 1700 A.D.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Religious movements which expect that the
      <a href="/wiki/Parousia" title="Parousia">
       second coming of Christ
      </a>
      as a cataclysmic event are generally called
      <i>
       adventism
      </i>
      . These have arisen throughout the Christian era, but were particularly common after the
      <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">
       Protestant Reformation
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Swedenborg" title="Emanuel Swedenborg">
       Emanuel Swedenborg
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Shakers" title="Shakers">
       Shakers
      </a>
      considered the second coming to be symbolic, and to have occurred in 1757. Along with others, he developed a religious systems around the second coming of Christ, disclosed by new prophecy or special revelation. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Millerites" title="Millerites">
       Millerites
      </a>
      are diverse religious groups which similarly rely upon a special gift of interpretation for predicting the second coming.
     </p>
     <p>
      The difference between the 19th century Millerite and
      <a href="/wiki/Adventism" title="Adventism">
       Adventist
      </a>
      movements and contemporary prophecy is that
      <a href="/wiki/William_Miller_(preacher)" title="William Miller (preacher)">
       William Miller
      </a>
      and his followers, based on Biblical interpretation, predicted the time of the Second Coming in 1844. Contemporary writing of end time has suggested that the timetable will be triggered by future wars and
      <a href="/wiki/Moral_panic" title="Moral panic">
       moral catastrophe
      </a>
      , and that this time of tribulation is close at hand.
     </p>
     <p>
      Seventh-day Adventists believe Biblical prophecy to foretell an end time scenario in which the United States works in conjunction with the Catholic Church to mandate worship on a day other than the true Sabbath, Saturday, as prescribed in the Ten Commandments (Exodus 20:811). This will bring about a situation where one must choose for or against the Bible as the will of God.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h5>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Preterism">
       Preterism
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Preterism">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h5>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Preterism" title="Preterism">
       Preterism
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Another view of the 'end times' known as
      <i>
       preterism
      </i>
      differentiates between the concept of 'time of the end' and 'end of time', and promotes a different understanding of these prophecies. The belief system suggests that the time of the end took place in the 1st century, more specifically AD 70, when the Jewish Temple was destroyed and animal sacrifices were stopped. In this view, the 'time of the end' refers to the
      <a href="/wiki/Antinomianism" title="Antinomianism">
       end of the covenant between God and Israel
      </a>
      , rather than the end of time or human life.
     </p>
     <p>
      Preterists believe that prophecies such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Coming" title="Second Coming">
       Second Coming
      </a>
      , the defiling of the Temple, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Destruction_of_Jerusalem" title="Destruction of Jerusalem">
       destruction of Jerusalem
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Antichrist" title="Antichrist">
       Antichrist
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Tribulation" title="Great Tribulation">
       Great Tribulation
      </a>
      , the advent of
      <a href="/wiki/The_Day_of_the_Lord" title="The Day of the Lord">
       The Day of the Lord
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Last_Judgment" title="Last Judgment">
       Final Judgment
      </a>
      were fulfilled at or about the year AD 70 when the Roman general and future Emperor
      <a href="/wiki/Titus" title="Titus">
       Titus
      </a>
      sacked
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
       Jerusalem
      </a>
      , destroyed the Temple, and put a stop to its daily animal sacrifices.
     </p>
     <p>
      Proponents of full preterism do not believe in a bodily
      <a href="/wiki/Resurrection_of_the_dead" title="Resurrection of the dead">
       resurrection of the dead
      </a>
      and place this event as well as the Second Coming in AD 70. Advocates of
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Partial_preterism" title="Partial preterism">
        partial preterism
       </a>
      </i>
      , in distinction, do believe in a coming resurrection. Full preterists contend that those who consider themselves to be partial preterists are actually just futurists, since they believe the Second Coming, Resurrection, Rapture and Judgment are still to come.
     </p>
     <p>
      Many preterists believe the 1st-century living Christians experienced the rapture to rejoin Christ. Preterists also believe the term 'Last Days' or 'Time of the End' refers not to the last days of planet Earth, or last days of mankind, but to the last days of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Covenant" title="Old Covenant">
       Old Covenant
      </a>
      , the Mosaic Covenant which God had exclusively with Israel until the year AD 70. In this belief, many 'time passages' in the
      <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">
       New Testament
      </a>
      are interpreted to foretell the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Coming" title="Second Coming">
       Second Coming
      </a>
      of Christ and Last Days to take place in the lifetimes of the disciples of Christ:
      <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Matthew" title="Gospel of Matthew">
       Matt.
      </a>
      10:23,
      <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Matthew" title="Gospel of Matthew">
       Matt.
      </a>
      16:28,
      <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Matthew" title="Gospel of Matthew">
       Matt.
      </a>
      24:34,
      <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Matthew" title="Gospel of Matthew">
       Matt.
      </a>
      26:64,
      <a href="/wiki/Epistle_to_the_Romans" title="Epistle to the Romans">
       Rom.
      </a>
      13:1112,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_Corinthians" title="1 Corinthians">
       1 Cor.
      </a>
      7:2931,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_Corinthians" title="1 Corinthians">
       1 Cor.
      </a>
      10:11,
      <a href="/wiki/Epistle_to_the_Philippians" title="Epistle to the Philippians">
       Phil.
      </a>
      4:5,
      <a href="/wiki/Epistle_of_James" title="Epistle of James">
       James
      </a>
      5:89,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_Peter" title="1 Peter">
       1 Pet.
      </a>
      4:7,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_John" title="1 John">
       1 Jn.
      </a>
      2:18.
     </p>
     <h5>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Dispensationalist_prophecies">
       Dispensationalist prophecies
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Dispensationalist prophecies">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h5>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Dispensationalism" title="Dispensationalism">
       Dispensationalism
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Christian_Zionism" title="Christian Zionism">
       Christian Zionism
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Israel_-Independence_May_14,_1948.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="419" data-file-width="426" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Israel_-Independence_May_14%2C_1948.jpg/220px-Israel_-Independence_May_14%2C_1948.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Israel_-Independence_May_14%2C_1948.jpg/330px-Israel_-Independence_May_14%2C_1948.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0a/Israel_-Independence_May_14%2C_1948.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Israel_-Independence_May_14,_1948.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A celebratory crowd gathered in
        <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">
         Tel Aviv
        </a>
        to hear the Declaration of Independence. The reestablishment of Israel provided impetus to
        <a href="/wiki/Dispensationalism" title="Dispensationalism">
         dispensationalism
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Dispensationalism is an
      <a href="/wiki/Evangelica" title="Evangelica">
       evangelica
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Futurist" title="Futurist">
       futurist
      </a>
      Bibilical interpretation that foresees a series of
      <a href="/wiki/Dispensation_(period)" title="Dispensation (period)">
       dispensations
      </a>
      , or periods, in which God relates to human beings under different
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biblical_covenants" title="Biblical covenants">
       Biblical covenants
      </a>
      . The belief system is primarily rooted in the writings of
      <a href="/wiki/John_Nelson_Darby" title="John Nelson Darby">
       John Nelson Darby
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Premillennial" title="Premillennial">
       premillennial
      </a>
      in content. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_(Israel)" title="Declaration of Independence (Israel)">
       reestablishment of Israel
      </a>
      in 1948 provided a major impetus to the dispensationalist belief system. The wars of Israel after 1948 with its Arab neighbors provided further support, according to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_F._Walvoord" title="John F. Walvoord">
       John F. Walvoord
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Six_Day_War" title="Six Day War">
       Six Day War
      </a>
      in 1967, and the
      <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War" title="Yom Kippur War">
       Yom Kippur War
      </a>
      in 1973, it seemed plausible to many
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fundamentalist_Christians" title="Fundamentalist Christians">
       Fundamentalist Christians
      </a>
      in the 1970s that Middle East turmoil may well be leading up to the fulfillment of various Bible prophecies and to the Battle of
      <a href="/wiki/Armageddon" title="Armageddon">
       Armageddon
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Members of the dispensationalist movement such as
      <a href="/wiki/Hal_Lindsey" title="Hal Lindsey">
       Hal Lindsey
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/J._Dwight_Pentecost" title="J. Dwight Pentecost">
       J. Dwight Pentecost
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/John_Walvoord" title="John Walvoord">
       John Walvoord
      </a>
      , all of whom have
      <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Theological_Seminary" title="Dallas Theological Seminary">
       Dallas Theological Seminary
      </a>
      backgrounds, and some other writers, claimed further that the
      <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">
       European Economic Community
      </a>
      , which preceded the
      <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
       European Union
      </a>
      , would become a
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Europe" title="United States of Europe">
       United States of Europe
      </a>
      , which would in turn become a Revived Roman Empire ruled by the
      <a href="/wiki/Antichrist" title="Antichrist">
       Antichrist
      </a>
      . The Revived Roman Empire also figured into the
      <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">
       New Testament
      </a>
      writers' vision of the future. The fact that in the early 1970s, there were (erroneously thought to be) seven nations in the European Economic Community was held to be significant; this aligned the Community with a seven-headed beast mentioned in Revelation. This specific prophecy has required revision, but the idea of a Revived Roman Empire remains.
     </p>
     <p>
      The separate destinies of the Church and Israel, a belief which is inherent in
      <a href="/wiki/Dispensationalism" title="Dispensationalism">
       dispensationalism
      </a>
      is a particular concern to some Jews and evangelical Christians. Evangelicals who reject dispensationalism, such as those who hold to a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post_Tribulation_Rapture" title="Post Tribulation Rapture">
       Post Tribulation Rapture
      </a>
      , (or more accurately a Post Tribulation Resurrection-Rapture), see both the Church and Israel entering the crucible of the End Time together.
      <span class="citation web">
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.voltairenet.org/article144310.html" rel="nofollow">
        "The Jerusalem Declaration on Christian Zionism"
       </a>
       . Riah Abu El-Assal, Swerios Malki Mourad, His Beatitude Michel Sabbah, Bishop Dr. Munib Younan.
      </span>
      <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEnd+time&amp;rft.btitle=The+Jerusalem+Declaration+on+Christian+Zionism&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.voltairenet.org%2Farticle144310.html&amp;rft.pub=Riah+Abu+El-Assal%2C+Swerios+Malki+Mourad%2C+His+Beatitude+Michel+Sabbah%2C+Bishop+Dr.+Munib+Younan&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
       <span style="display:none;">
       </span>
      </span>
     </p>
     <p>
      Dispensationalism, in contrast to the Millerite Adventist movement, had its beginning in the 19th century, when
      <a href="/wiki/John_Nelson_Darby" title="John Nelson Darby">
       John Nelson Darby
      </a>
      , founder of the
      <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Brethren" title="Plymouth Brethren">
       Plymouth Brethren
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Religious_denomination" title="Religious denomination">
       religious denomination
      </a>
      , incorporated into his system of Biblical interpretation a system of organizing Biblical time into a number of discrete
      <a href="/wiki/Dispensation_(period)" title="Dispensation (period)">
       dispensations
      </a>
      , each of which marks a separate
      <a href="/wiki/Covenant_(religion)" title="Covenant (religion)">
       covenant
      </a>
      with God. Darby's beliefs were widely publicized in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyrus_I._Scofield" title="Cyrus I. Scofield">
       Cyrus I. Scofield
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Scofield_Reference_Bible" title="Scofield Reference Bible">
        Scofield Reference Bible
       </a>
      </i>
      , an annotated Bible that became popular in the United States of America.
     </p>
     <p>
      Since the majority of the Biblical prophets were writing at a time when the
      <a href="/wiki/Temple_in_Jerusalem" title="Temple in Jerusalem">
       Temple in Jerusalem
      </a>
      was still functioning, they wrote as if it would still be standing during the prophesied events. According to preterism, this was a fulfillment of the prophecies. However, according to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Futurism_(Christian_eschatology)" title="Futurism (Christian eschatology)">
       Futurists
      </a>
      , their destruction in AD 70 put the prophetic timetable on hold. Many such believers therefore anticipated the return of Jews to Israel and the
      <a href="/wiki/Third_Temple#Christian_views" title="Third Temple">
       reconstruction of the Temple
      </a>
      before the Second Coming could occur.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h5>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-tribulation_pre-millennialists">
       Post-tribulation pre-millennialists
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Post-tribulation pre-millennialists">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h5>
     <p>
      A view of the Second Coming of Christ as held by post-tribulational pre-millennialists is unique, though not widely held in the Protestant Church because of its connotations, in particular that the Church of Christ will have to undergo great persecution.
     </p>
     <h5>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Specific_prophetic_movements">
       Specific prophetic movements
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Specific prophetic movements">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h5>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Disappointment" title="Great Disappointment">
       Great Disappointment
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:William_Miller.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="364" data-file-width="249" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/William_Miller.jpg/120px-William_Miller.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/William_Miller.jpg/180px-William_Miller.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/William_Miller.jpg/240px-William_Miller.jpg 2x" width="120"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:William_Miller.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        William Miller predicted the end of the world in 1843, known as the
        <a href="/wiki/Great_Disappointment" title="Great Disappointment">
         Great Disappointment
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1843,
      <a href="/wiki/William_Miller_(preacher)" title="William Miller (preacher)">
       William Miller
      </a>
      made the first of several predictions that the world would end in only a few months. As his predictions did not come true (referred to as the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Disappointment" title="Great Disappointment">
       Great Disappointment
      </a>
      ),
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Millerites" title="Millerites">
       followers of Miller
      </a>
      went on to found separate groups, the most successful of which is the
      <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">
       Seventh-day Adventist Church
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Members of the
      <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bah' Faith">
       Bah' Faith
      </a>
      believe that Miller's interpretation of signs and dates of the coming of Jesus were, for the most part, correct.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-momen_29-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-momen-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They believe that the fulfillment of biblical prophecies of the coming of Christ came through a forerunner of their own religion, the
      <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1b" title="Bb">
       Bb
      </a>
      . According to the Bb's words, 4 April 1844 was "the first day that the Spirit descended" into his heart.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Momen_2007_71.E2.80.9388_30-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Momen_2007_71.E2.80.9388-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His subsequent declaration to
      <a href="/wiki/Mull%C3%A1_Husayn" title="Mull Husayn">
       Mull Husayn-i Bushru'i
      </a>
      that he was the "Promised One"an event now commemorated by Bah's as a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ascension_of_Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Ascension of Bah'u'llh">
       major holy day
      </a>
      took place on 23 May 1844. It was in October of that year that the Bb embarked on a
      <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">
       pilgrimage to Mecca
      </a>
      , where he openly declared his claims to the
      <a href="/wiki/Sharif_of_Mecca" title="Sharif of Mecca">
       Sharif of Mecca
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chron_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Chron-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gpb_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-gpb-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first news coverage of these events in the West was in 1845 by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">
        The Times
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Momen_1999_online_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Momen_1999_online-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      followed by others in 1850 in the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bah.C3.A1.27.C3.AD_Library_Online_34-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bah.C3.A1.27.C3.AD_Library_Online-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first Bah' to come to America was in 1892.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chron_31-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Chron-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Several Bah' books and pamphlets make mention of the Millerites, the prophecies used by Miller and the Great Disappointment, most notably
      <a href="/wiki/William_Sears_(Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD)" title="William Sears (Bah')">
       William Sears
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       Thief in the Night
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sears_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sears-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowers_2004_12_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bowers_2004_12-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Motlagh_1992_205.E2.80.93213_37-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Motlagh_1992_205.E2.80.93213-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Restorationism_.28Christian_primitivism.29">
       Restorationism (Christian primitivism)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Restorationism (Christian primitivism)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      End times theology is also significant to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Restorationism_(Christian_primitivism)" title="Restorationism (Christian primitivism)">
       restorationist
      </a>
      Christian religions, which consider themselves distinct from both Catholicism and Protestantism.
     </p>
     <h5>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Jehovah.27s_Witnesses">
       Jehovah's Witnesses
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Jehovah's Witnesses">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h5>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Eschatology_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Eschatology of Jehovah's Witnesses">
       Eschatology of Jehovah's Witnesses
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Watchtower_Bible_%26_Tract_Society_(world_headquarters).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2478" data-file-width="3716" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Watchtower_Bible_%26_Tract_Society_%28world_headquarters%29.jpg/300px-Watchtower_Bible_%26_Tract_Society_%28world_headquarters%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Watchtower_Bible_%26_Tract_Society_%28world_headquarters%29.jpg/450px-Watchtower_Bible_%26_Tract_Society_%28world_headquarters%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Watchtower_Bible_%26_Tract_Society_%28world_headquarters%29.jpg/600px-Watchtower_Bible_%26_Tract_Society_%28world_headquarters%29.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Watchtower_Bible_%26_Tract_Society_(world_headquarters).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Current Watch Tower headquarters in
        <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">
         Brooklyn
        </a>
        . The society made a number of emphatic claims of impending last days and ensuing chaos between 18791924.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Eschatology" title="Eschatology">
       eschatology
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">
       Jehovah's Witnesses
      </a>
      is central to their religious beliefs. They believe that
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ" title="Jesus Christ">
       Jesus Christ
      </a>
      has been ruling in heaven as king since 1914 (a date they believe was prophesied in Scripture), and that after that time a period of cleansing occurred, resulting in God's selection of the
      <a href="/wiki/Bible_Student_movement" title="Bible Student movement">
       Bible Students
      </a>
      associated with
      <a href="/wiki/Charles_Taze_Russell" title="Charles Taze Russell">
       Charles Taze Russell
      </a>
      to be his people in 1919. They also believe the destruction of those who reject their message
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and thus willfully refuse to obey God
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      will shortly take place at
      <a href="/wiki/Armageddon#Jehovah.27s_Witnesses" title="Armageddon">
       Armageddon
      </a>
      , ensuring that the beginning of the new earthly society will be composed of willing subjects of that kingdom.
     </p>
     <p>
      The religion's doctrines surrounding 1914 are the legacy of a series of emphatic claims regarding the years 1799,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indisputable_41-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-indisputable-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      1874,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indisputable_41-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-indisputable-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      1878,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OurFaith1875_42-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-OurFaith1875-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      1914,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheWatchtower_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-TheWatchtower-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      1918
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-September_44-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-September-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and 1925
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MillionsNow_45-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-MillionsNow-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      made in the
      <a href="/wiki/Watch_Tower_Bible_and_Tract_Society_of_Pennsylvania" title="Watch Tower Bible and Tract Society of Pennsylvania">
       Watch Tower Society's
      </a>
      publications between 1879 and 1924. Claims about the significance of those years, including the presence of Jesus Christ, the beginning of the "
