      <a href="/wiki/End_time#Jehovah.27s_Witnesses" title="End time">
       last days
      </a>
      ", the destruction of worldly governments and the earthly resurrection of Jewish patriarchs, were successively abandoned.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1922 the society's principal journal,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Watchtower" title="The Watchtower">
        The Watchtower
       </a>
      </i>
      , described its chronology as "no stronger than its weakest link", but also claimed the chronological relationships to be "of divine origin and divinely corroborated...in a class by itself, absolutely and unqualifiedly correct"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and "indisputable facts",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indisputable_41-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-indisputable-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while repudiation of Russell's teachings was described as "equivalent to a repudiation of the Lord".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Watch Tower Society has admitted its early leaders promoted "incomplete, even inaccurate concepts".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Governing_Body_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Governing Body of Jehovah's Witnesses">
       Governing Body of Jehovah's Witnesses
      </a>
      says that, unlike
      <a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">
       Old Testament
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Prophet#Judaism" title="Prophet">
       prophets
      </a>
      , its interpretations of the Bible are not
      <a href="/wiki/Biblical_inspiration" title="Biblical inspiration">
       inspired
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Biblical_infallibility" title="Biblical infallibility">
       infallible
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_publications" title="Jehovah's Witnesses publications">
       Witness publications
      </a>
      say that Bible prophecies can be fully understood only after their fulfillment, citing examples of biblical figures who did not understand the meaning of prophecies they received. Watch Tower publications often cite Proverbs 4:18, "The path of the righteous ones is like the bright light that is getting lighter and lighter until the day is firmly established" (
      <a href="/wiki/New_World_Translation_of_the_Holy_Scriptures" title="New World Translation of the Holy Scriptures">
       NWT
      </a>
      ) to support their view that there would be an increase in knowledge during "the time of the end", as mentioned in Daniel 12:4. Jehovah's Witnesses state that this increase in knowledge needs adjustments. Watch Tower publications also say that unfulfilled expectations are partly due to eagerness for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/God%27s_Kingdom" title="God's Kingdom">
       God's Kingdom
      </a>
      and that they do not call
      <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_beliefs" title="Jehovah's Witnesses beliefs">
       their core beliefs
      </a>
      into question.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h5>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints">
       The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h5>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Coming_(LDS_Church)" title="Second Coming (LDS Church)">
       Second Coming (LDS Church)
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Members of
      <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
       The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
      </a>
      believe that there will be a Second Coming of Jesus to the earth sometime in the future. The LDS Church and its leaders do not make any predictions of the actual date of the Second Coming.
     </p>
     <p>
      According to church teaching, the true
      <a href="/wiki/Gospel" title="Gospel">
       gospel
      </a>
      will be taught in all parts of the world prior to the Second Coming.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matthew_24:14_56-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Matthew_24:14-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They also believe that there will be increasing war, earthquakes, hurricanes, and man-made disasters prior to the Second Coming.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Islam">
       Islam
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Islam">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Islamic_eschatology" title="Islamic eschatology">
       Islamic eschatology
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Muslims believe that there are three periods before the Day of Judgment, also known as
      <i>
       ashratu's-sa'ah
      </i>
      or
      <i>
       alamatu qiyami's-sa'ah,
      </i>
      with some debate as to whether the periods could overlap.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mahdi2_58-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mahdi2-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joel_59-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Joel-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hooper_60-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hooper-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The first period is said to have begun with the death of Muhammad. The second began with the passing of all his Companions, and ended a thousand years later. Another event of the second period was the Tartar invasion, occurring 650 years after Muhammad. The Mongols, led by
      <a href="/wiki/Hulagu_Khan" title="Hulagu Khan">
       Hulagu Khan
      </a>
      , grandson of
      <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">
       Genghis Khan
      </a>
      , attacked Baghdad in 1258 AD and brought the Abbasid caliphate to an end. They massacred millions of Muslims, and the water of the river Tigris turned red with blood. The Qur'an also predicted a fire at Madinah in the Hijaz near
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Busra" title="Busra">
       Busra
      </a>
      in Syria, which Islamic scholars believe occurred in 654 AH.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mahdi2_58-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mahdi2-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Following the second, the third and final period will be heralded by the appearance of the Mahdi.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mahdi2_58-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mahdi2-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sunni">
       Sunni
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sunni">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Sunnis believe that the dead will then stand in a grand assembly, awaiting a scroll detailing their righteous deeds, sinful acts and ultimate judgment.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-muhammad59_62-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-muhammad59-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">
       Muhammad
      </a>
      will be the first to be resurrected.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Punishments will include
      <i>
       adhab
      </i>
      , or severe pain and embarrassment, and
      <i>
       khizy
      </i>
      or shame.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WimEoQ_64-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WimEoQ-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There will also be a punishment of the grave between death and the resurrection.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h5>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Major_signs">
       Major signs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Major signs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h5>
     <p>
      There are twelve major signs of
      <i>
       Qiyamah
      </i>
      , known as
      <i>
       amaratu's-sa'ah al- kubra
      </i>
      . The first sign will be the appearance of the imam, Mahdi, whose appearance is awaited by the angel
      <a href="/wiki/Islamic_view_of_angels" title="Islamic view of angels">
       Israfil
      </a>
      , so that he may sound the horn signalling the end of days. The natural order will become reversed, including the sun, mountains and sea.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stone_66-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Stone-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The twelve signs are as follows:
     </p>
     <ol>
      <li>
       Rise (or
       <a href="/wiki/Occultation" title="Occultation">
        Occultation
       </a>
       in Shia belief) of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mahdi" title="Mahdi">
         Mahdi
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joel_59-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Joel-59">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         59
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stone_66-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Stone-66">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         66
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       The false messiah,
       <a href="/wiki/Masih_ad-Dajjal" title="Masih ad-Dajjal">
        Masih ad-Dajjal
       </a>
       , shall appear as a creature with one eye good and the other blind, and the mark of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Kafir" title="Kafir">
         Kafir
        </a>
       </i>
       . He will claim to hold keys to heaven and hell and lead many astray, although believers will not be deceived.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hooper_60-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hooper-60">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         60
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         67
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Medina will be deserted, with true believers going to follow Mahdi and sinners following Dajjal
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Jesus_in_Islam" title="Jesus in Islam">
        Isa
       </a>
       , or Jesus, shall return from the seventh sky to assist the Mahdi against Dajjal
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         68
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Gog_and_Magog" title="Gog and Magog">
        <i>
         Ya'jooj
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         Ma'jooj
        </i>
       </a>
       , two tribes of vicious beings which had been imprisoned will escape. They will ravage the earth, drink all its water, and destroy all life. Allah will then send worms and insects to destroy them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hooper_60-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hooper-60">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         60
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         69
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         70
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       The sun will rise from the west.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         71
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         72
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         73
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       At this point, it is useless for humans want to atone their sins
      </li>
      <li>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Beast_of_the_Earth" title="Beast of the Earth">
        Beast of the Earth
       </a>
       , or
       <i>
        Dabbat al-ard
       </i>
       , will populate the entire planet
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         74
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Beast will mark every people on earth based on their beliefs (believers or unbelievers)
      </li>
      <li>
       The Qur'an will be taken to heaven and even the
       <a href="/wiki/Hafiz_(Quran)" title="Hafiz (Quran)">
        Hafiz
       </a>
       will not recall its verses
      </li>
      <li>
       A pleasant breeze will blow from Yemen that will cause all believers to die peacefully, leaving the Earth with the wicked unbelievers
      </li>
      <li>
       A short legged and thin ruler of Ethiopia will attack Mecca and destroy the
       <a href="/wiki/Kaaba" title="Kaaba">
        Kaaba
       </a>
       , and throw its stones to the sea
      </li>
      <li>
       A first trumpet will sound, and all remaining humanity will die, followed by a period of forty years, at the end of which smoke will envelop the world for forty days
      </li>
      <li>
       A second trumpet will sound, the dead will return to life, and a fire will start from Hadramawt in Yemen that shall gather all people of the world in Mahshar for the Last Judgment
      </li>
     </ol>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Shia">
       Shia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Shia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Concepts and terminology in Shia eschatology includes
      <a href="/wiki/Mi%27ad" title="Mi'ad">
       Mi'ad
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/The_Occultation" title="The Occultation">
       The Occultation
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Al-Yamani_(Shiism)" title="Al-Yamani (Shiism)">
       Al-Yamani
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Sufyani" title="Sufyani">
       Sufyani
      </a>
      In Twelver Shia hadiths about the last days, the literature largely revolves around
      <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_al-Mahdi" title="Muhammad al-Mahdi">
       Muhammad al-Mahdi
      </a>
      , a messianic figure considered to be the twelfth appointed successor to Muhammad. Mahdi will help mankind against the deception by a man called
      <i>
       Dajjal
      </i>
      who will try to woe (woo?) people to a new world religion which is called "the great deception".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Ahmadiyya">
       Ahmadiyya
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Ahmadiyya">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">
       Ahmadiyya
      </a>
      is considered distinct from mainstream Islam. In its writing, the present age has been witness to the evil of man and wrath of God, with war and natural disaster.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Mirza_Ghulam_Ahmad" title="Mirza Ghulam Ahmad">
       Ghulam Ahmad
      </a>
      is seen as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_coming" title="Second coming">
       promised Messiah
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Mahdi" title="Mahdi">
       Mahdi
      </a>
      , fulfilling Islamic and Biblical prophecies, as well as scriptures of other religions such as Hinduism. His teaching will establish spiritual reform and establish an age of peace. This will continue for a thousand years, and will unify mankind under one faith.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Ahmadis believe that despite harsh and strong opposition and discrimination they will eventually be triumphant and their message vindicated both by Muslims and non-Muslims alike. Ahmadis also incorporate the eschatological views from other religions into their doctrine and believe that Mirza Ghulam Ahmed falls into this sequence.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Bah.C3.A1.27.C3.AD_Faith">
       Bah' Faith
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Bah' Faith">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The founder of the
      <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bah' Faith">
       Bah' Faith
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Bah'u'llh">
       Bah'u'llh
      </a>
      claimed that he was the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Coming" title="Second Coming">
       return of Christ
      </a>
      as well as prophetic expectations of other religions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The inception of the Bah' Faith coincides with
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Disappointment" title="Great Disappointment">
       Millerite prophesy
      </a>
      , pointing to the year 1844. They also believe the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Armageddon" title="Battle of Armageddon">
       Battle of Armageddon
      </a>
      has passed and that the mass martyrdom anticipated during the
      <i>
       End Times
      </i>
      had already passed within the
      <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%ADs#Historical_context" title="Persecution of Bah's">
       historical context
      </a>
      of the Bah' Faith.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Bah's expect their faith to be eventually embraced by the masses of the world, ushering in a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_age" title="Golden age">
       golden age
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Rastafari_movement">
       Rastafari movement
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Rastafari movement">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rastafari_movement" title="Rastafari movement">
       Rastafari movement
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Selassie_restored.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3257" data-file-width="2494" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Selassie_restored.jpg/170px-Selassie_restored.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Selassie_restored.jpg/255px-Selassie_restored.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Selassie_restored.jpg/340px-Selassie_restored.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Selassie_restored.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haile_Selassie_I" title="Haile Selassie I">
         Haile Selassie I
        </a>
        is viewed as god incarnate in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rastafarianism" title="Rastafarianism">
         Rastafarianism
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Rastafarians have a unique interpretation of end times, based on the
      <a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">
       Old Testament
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Revelation" title="Book of Revelation">
       Book of Revelation
      </a>
      . They believe
      <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">
       Ethiopian
      </a>
      Emperor
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haile_Selassie_I" title="Haile Selassie I">
       Haile Selassie I
      </a>
      to be God
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Incarnate" title="Incarnate">
       incarnate
      </a>
      , the
      <i>
       King of kings
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       Lord of lords
      </i>
      mentioned in Revelation 5:5. They saw the crowning of Selassie as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_coming" title="Second coming">
       second coming
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Italo-Ethiopian_War" title="Second Italo-Ethiopian War">
       Second Italo-Ethiopian War
      </a>
      as fulfillment of Revelation. There is also the expectation that Selassie will return for a day of judgment and bring home the lost children of Israel, which in Rastafarianism refer to those taken from Africa through the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">
       slave trade
      </a>
      . There will then be an era of peace and harmony at Mount
      <a href="/wiki/Zion" title="Zion">
       Zion
      </a>
      in Africa.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown_82-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Brown-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cyclic_cosmology">
       Cyclic cosmology
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cyclic cosmology">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Norse_religion">
       Norse religion
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Norse religion">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Ragnar%C3%B6k" title="Ragnark">
       Ragnark
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Odin_und_Fenriswolf_Freyr_und_Surt.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1038" data-file-width="1690" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Odin_und_Fenriswolf_Freyr_und_Surt.jpg/220px-Odin_und_Fenriswolf_Freyr_und_Surt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Odin_und_Fenriswolf_Freyr_und_Surt.jpg/330px-Odin_und_Fenriswolf_Freyr_und_Surt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Odin_und_Fenriswolf_Freyr_und_Surt.jpg/440px-Odin_und_Fenriswolf_Freyr_und_Surt.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Odin_und_Fenriswolf_Freyr_und_Surt.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Odin fighting his old nemesis
        <a href="/wiki/Fenrir" title="Fenrir">
         Fenrir
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Norse_mythology" title="Norse mythology">
       Norse mythology
      </a>
      depicts the end of days as
      <i>
       Ragnark
      </i>
      , an
      <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">
       Old Norse
      </a>
      term translatable as "twilight of the Gods". It will be heralded by a devastation known as
      <a href="/wiki/Fimbulwinter" title="Fimbulwinter">
       Fimbulwinter
      </a>
      which will seize
      <a href="/wiki/Midgard" title="Midgard">
       Midgard
      </a>
      in cold and darkness. The sun and moon will disappear from the sky, and poison will fill the air. Dead will rise from the ground and there will be widespread despair.
     </p>
     <p>
      There follows a battle between - on the one hand - the Gods with the
      <a href="/wiki/%C3%86sir" title="sir">
       sir
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Vanir" title="Vanir">
       Vanir
      </a>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Einherjar" title="Einherjar">
       Einherjar
      </a>
      , led by
      <a href="/wiki/Odin" title="Odin">
       Odin
      </a>
      , and - on the other hand - forces of Chaos, including the fire giants and
      <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B6tunn" title="Jtunn">
       jtunn
      </a>
      , led by
      <a href="/wiki/Loki" title="Loki">
       Loki
      </a>
      . In the fighting
      <a href="/wiki/Odin" title="Odin">
       Odin
      </a>
      will be swallowed whole by his old nemesis
      <a href="/wiki/Fenrir" title="Fenrir">
       Fenrir
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LARRINGTON266_83-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-LARRINGTON266-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The god
      <a href="/wiki/Freyr" title="Freyr">
       Freyr
      </a>
      fights
      <a href="/wiki/Surtr" title="Surtr">
       Surtr
      </a>
      but loses.
      <a href="/wiki/V%C3%AD%C3%B0arr" title="Varr">
       Varr
      </a>
      , son of Odin, will then avenge his father by ripping Fenrir's jaws apart and stabbing the wolf in the heart with his spear. The serpent
      <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B6rmungandr" title="Jrmungandr">
       Jrmungandr
      </a>
      will open its gaping maw and be met in combat by
      <a href="/wiki/Thor" title="Thor">
       Thor
      </a>
      . Thor, also a son of Odin, will defeat the serpent, only to take nine steps afterwards before collapsing to his own death.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After this people will flee their homes as the sun blackens and the earth sinks into the sea. The stars will vanish, steam will rise, and flames will touch the heavens. This conflict will result in the deaths of most of the major Gods and forces of Chaos. Finally,
      <a href="/wiki/Surtr" title="Surtr">
       Surtr
      </a>
      will fling fire across the nine worlds. The ocean will then completely submerge
      <a href="/wiki/Midgard" title="Midgard">
       Midgard
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After the cataclysm the world will resurface new and fertile, and the surviving Gods will meet. The two human survivors,
      <a href="/wiki/L%C3%ADf_and_L%C3%ADf%C3%BErasir" title="Lf and Lfrasir">
       Lf and Lfrasir
      </a>
      , will then repopulate this new earth.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Odin_86-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Odin-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ragnar%C3%B6k_by_Doepler.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1290" data-file-width="1634" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ragnar%C3%B6k_by_Doepler.jpg/170px-Ragnar%C3%B6k_by_Doepler.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ragnar%C3%B6k_by_Doepler.jpg/255px-Ragnar%C3%B6k_by_Doepler.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ragnar%C3%B6k_by_Doepler.jpg/340px-Ragnar%C3%B6k_by_Doepler.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ragnar%C3%B6k_by_Doepler.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Ragnark after Surtr has engulfed the world with fire
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Hinduism">
       Hinduism
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Hinduism">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Hindu_eschatology" title="Hindu eschatology">
       Hindu eschatology
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Kalki" title="Kalki">
       Kalki
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Hindu_eschatology" title="Hindu eschatology">
       Hindu eschatology
      </a>
      , time is cyclic and consists of
      <a href="/wiki/Kalpa_(aeon)" title="Kalpa (aeon)">
       kalpas
      </a>
      . Each lasts 4.1  8.2 billion years, which is a period of one full day and night for
      <a href="/wiki/Brahma" title="Brahma">
       Brahma
      </a>
      , who will be alive for 311 trillion, 40 billion years. Within a
      <i>
       kalpa
      </i>
      there are periods of
      <a href="/wiki/Brahma" title="Brahma">
       creation
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Vishnu" title="Vishnu">
       preservation
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Shiva" title="Shiva">
       decline
      </a>
      . After this larger cycle, all of creation will contract to a
      <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_singularity" title="Gravitational singularity">
       singularity
      </a>
      and then again will expand from that single point, as the
      <a href="/wiki/Yuga" title="Yuga">
       ages
      </a>
      continue in a religious
      <a href="/wiki/Fractal" title="Fractal">
       fractal
      </a>
      pattern.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hooper_60-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hooper-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Within the current kalpa, there are four epochs that encompass the cycle. They progress from a beginning of complete purity to a descent into total corruption. The last of the four ages is
      <a href="/wiki/Kali_Yuga" title="Kali Yuga">
       Kali Yuga
      </a>
      , our current time, during which will be characterized by impiety, violence and decay. The four pillars of dharma will be reduced to one, with truth being all that remains.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As written in the
      <a href="/wiki/Bhagavad_Gita" title="Bhagavad Gita">
       Gita
      </a>
      :
     </p>
     <div class="poem">
      <p>
       <span class="mw-poem-indented" style="display: inline-block; margin-left: 2em;">
        Yad yad hi dharmasya glnirbhavati Bhrata
       </span>
       <br/>
       <span class="mw-poem-indented" style="display: inline-block; margin-left: 2em;">
        Abhyutthnam adharmasya tadtmnam sjmyaham
       </span>
       <br/>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <br/>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       <span class="mw-poem-indented" style="display: inline-block; margin-left: 2em;">
        Whenever there is decay of righteousness O! Bharata
       </span>
       <br/>
       <span class="mw-poem-indented" style="display: inline-block; margin-left: 2em;">
        And a rise of unrighteousness then I manifest Myself!
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
         <a href="#cite_note-88">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          88
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </span>
      </p>
     </div>
     <p>
      At this time of chaos, the final avatar,
      <a href="/wiki/Kalki" title="Kalki">
       Kalki
      </a>
      , endowed with eight superhuman faculties will appear on a white horse. Kalki will amass an army to "establish righteousness upon the earth" and leave "the minds of the people as pure as crystal."
     </p>
     <p>
      At the completion of
      <a href="/wiki/Kali_Yuga" title="Kali Yuga">
       Kali Yuga
      </a>
      , the next cycle will begin with a new
      <a href="/wiki/Satya_Yuga" title="Satya Yuga">
       Satya Yuga
      </a>
      , in which all will once again be righteous with the reestablishment of dharma. This, in turn, will be followed by epochs of Treta Yuga, Dwapara Yuga and again another Kali Yuga. This cycle will then repeat till the larger cycle of existence under
      <a href="/wiki/Brahma" title="Brahma">
       Brahma
      </a>
      returns to the
      <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_singularity" title="Gravitational singularity">
       singularity
      </a>
      , and a new universe is born.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown_82-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Brown-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Buddhism">
       Buddhism
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Buddhism">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_eschatology" title="Buddhist eschatology">
       Buddhist eschatology
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Maitreya" title="Maitreya">
       Maitreya
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      There are two major points of Buddhist eschatology, the appearance of
      <a href="/wiki/Maitreya" title="Maitreya">
       Maitreya
      </a>
      , followed by the Sermon of the Seven Suns.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Maitreya">
       Maitreya
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Maitreya">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Buddha described his teachings disappearing five thousand years from when he preached them, corresponding approximately to the year 2300. At this time, knowledge of
      <a href="/wiki/Dharma" title="Dharma">
       dharma
      </a>
      will be lost as well. The last of his relics will be gathered in Bodh Gaya and cremated.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2012)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      There will be a new era in which the next Buddha Maitreya will appear, but it will be preceded by the degeneration of human society. This will be a period of greed, lust, poverty, ill will, violence, murder, impiety, physical weakness, sexual depravity and societal collapse, and even the Buddha himself will be forgotten.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hooper_60-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hooper-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      This will be followed by the coming of Maitreya when the teachings of
      <a href="/wiki/Dharma" title="Dharma">
       dharma
      </a>
      are forgotten. Maitreya was the first bhoddisatva around whom a cult developed, in approximately the 3rd century CE.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brittanica_89-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Brittanica-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The earliest mention of Maitreya is in the Cakavatti, or Sihanada Sutta in
      <a href="/wiki/Digha_Nikaya" title="Digha Nikaya">
       Digha Nikaya
      </a>
      26 of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pali_Canon" title="Pali Canon">
       Pali Canon
      </a>
      . In it,
      <a href="/wiki/Gautama_Buddha" title="Gautama Buddha">
       Gautama Buddha
      </a>
      predicted that his teachings of dharma would be forgotten after 5,000 years.
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       At that period, brethren, there will arise in the world an Exalted One named Maitreya, Fully Awakened, abounding in wisdom and goodness, happy, with knowledge of the worlds, unsurpassed as a guide to mortals willing to be led, a teacher for gods and men, an Exalted One, a Buddha, even as I am now. He, by himself, will thoroughly know and see, as it were face to face, this universe, with Its worlds of the spirits, Its Brahmas and Its Maras, and Its world of recluses and Brahmins, of princes and peoples, even as I now, by myself, thoroughly know and see them
      </p>
      <div class="templatequotecite">
       Digha Nikaya, 26
      </div>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      Maitreya Buddha is then foretold to be born in the city of Ketumat in present-day Benares, whose king will be the Cakkavatt Sankha. Sankha will live in the former palace of King Mahpanad, and will become a renunciate who follows Maitreya.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In Mahayana Buddhism, Maitreya will attain
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Bodhi" title="Bodhi">
        bodhi
       </a>
      </i>
      in seven days, the minimum period, by virtue of his many lifetimes of preparation. Once Buddha, he will rule over the Ketumati Pure Land, an earthly paradise sometimes associated with the Indian city of
      <a href="/wiki/Varanasi" title="Varanasi">
       Varanasi
      </a>
      or Benares in Uttar Pradesh. In Mahayana Buddhism, the Buddha presides over a land of purity. For example,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amitabha" title="Amitabha">
       Amitabha
      </a>
      presides over Sukhavati, more popularly known as the 'Western Paradise'.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KushanMaitreya.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="269" height="397" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/KushanMaitreya.JPG/170px-KushanMaitreya.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/KushanMaitreya.JPG/255px-KushanMaitreya.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/59/KushanMaitreya.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KushanMaitreya.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Bodhisattva Maitreya from the 2nd Century Gandharan Art Period
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      A notable teaching he will rediscover is that of the ten non-virtuous deedskilling, stealing, sexual misconduct, lying, divisive speech, abusive speech, idle speech, covetousness, harmful intent and wrong views. These will be replaced by the ten virtuous deeds, which are the abandonment of each of these practices. He is described by Conze in his Buddhist Scriptures:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       The Lord replied, 'Maitreya, the best of men, will then leave the
       <a href="/wiki/Tushita" title="Tushita">
        <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration">
         Tuita
        </span>
       </a>
       heavens, and go for his last rebirth. As soon as he is born he will walk seven steps forward, and where he puts down his feet a jewel or a lotus will spring up. He will raise his eyes to the ten directions, and will speak these words: "This is my last birth. There will be no rebirth after this one. Never will I come back here, but, all pure, I shall win Nirvana."
      </p>
      <div class="templatequotecite">
       
       <i>
        Buddhist Scriptures
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         93
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </div>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      He currently resides in
      <a href="/wiki/Tushita" title="Tushita">
       Tushita
      </a>
      , but will come to
      <a href="/wiki/Jambudvipa" title="Jambudvipa">
       Jambudvipa
      </a>
      when needed most as successor to the historic
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C5%9A%C4%81kyamuni_Buddha" title="kyamuni Buddha">
       kyamuni Buddha
      </a>
      . Maitreya will achieve complete enlightenment during his lifetime, and following this reawakening, he will bring back the timeless teaching of
      <a href="/wiki/Dharma" title="Dharma">
       dharma
      </a>
      to this plane and rediscover
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nirvana_(concept)" title="Nirvana (concept)">
       enlightenment
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Theravada_Buddhism_1988.2C_pages_83-85_94-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Theravada_Buddhism_1988.2C_pages_83-85-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Arya_Maitreya_Mandala" title="Arya Maitreya Mandala">
       Arya Maitreya Mandala
      </a>
      , founded by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lama_Anagarika_Govinda" title="Lama Anagarika Govinda">
       Lama Anagarika Govinda
      </a>
      is based on the idea of Maitreya.
     </p>
     <p>
      Maitreya eschatology forms the central canon of the
      <a href="/wiki/Drikung_Kagyu" title="Drikung Kagyu">
       White Lotus Society
      </a>
      , a revolutionary movement during
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_imperialism" title="British imperialism">
       British colonial rule
      </a>
      . It later branched into the
      <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
       Chinese
      </a>
      underground criminal organization known as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Triad_(underground_society)" title="Triad (underground society)">
       Triad
      </a>
      , which exists today as an international underground criminal network.
     </p>
     <p>
      It is of note that description of Maitreya occurs in no other sutta in the canon, casting doubt as to authenticity of the scripture. In addition, sermons of the Buddha normally are in response to a question, or in a specific context, but this sutta has a beginning and an ending, and its content is quite different from the others. This has led some to conclude that the whole sutta is apocryphal, or tampered with.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Theravada_Buddhism_1988.2C_pages_83-85_94-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Theravada_Buddhism_1988.2C_pages_83-85-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sermon_of_the_Seven_Suns">
       Sermon of the Seven Suns
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=End_time&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sermon of the Seven Suns">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      In his "Sermon of the Seven Suns" in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pali_Canon" title="Pali Canon">
       Pali Canon
      </a>
      , the Buddha describes the ultimate fate of the world in an apocalypse that will be characterized by the consequent appearance of seven suns in the sky, each causing progressive ruin till the Earth is destroyed:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       All things are impermanent, all aspects of existence are unstable and non-eternal. Beings will become so weary and disgusted with the constituent things that they will seek emancipation from them more quickly. There will come a season, O monks when, after hundreds of thousands of years, rains will cease. All seedlings, all vegetation, all plants, grasses and trees will dry up and cease to be...There comes another season after a great lapse of time when a second sun will appear. Now all brooks and ponds will dry up, vanish, cease to be.
      </p>
      <div class="templatequotecite">
       Aguttara-Nikya, VII, 6.2 Pali Canon
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hooper_60-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hooper-60">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         60
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </div>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      The canon goes on to describe the progressive destruction of each sun. A third sun will dry the mighty
      <a href="/wiki/Ganges" title="Ganges">
       Ganges
      </a>
      and other great rivers. A fourth will cause the great lakes to evaporate, and a fifth will dry the oceans. Finally:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       Again after a vast period of time a sixth sun will appear, and it will bake the Earth even as a pot is baked by a potter. All the mountains will reek and send up clouds of smoke. After another great interval a seventh sun will appear and the Earth will blaze with fire until it becomes one mass of flame. The mountains will be consumed, a spark will be carried on the wind and go to the worlds of God....Thus, monks, all things will burn, perish and exist no more except those who have seen the path.
      </p>
      <div class="templatequotecite">
       
       <cite>
        Aguttara-Nikya, VII, 6.2 Pali Canon
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hooper_60-6">
         <a href="#cite_note-Hooper-60">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          60
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </cite>
      </div>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      The sermon completes with the planet engulfed by a vast inferno. The Pali Canon does not indicate when this will happen relative to Maitreya.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hooper_60-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hooper-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">

          </a>

Some of them are of so remarkable a character as clearly to indicate that this chronology is not of man, but of God. Being of divine origin and divinely corroborated, present-truth chronology stands in a class by itself, absolutely and unqualifiedly correct."
